Wait — let me think about this more carefully. For front camera, sensor_orientation = 270. Let me check what Option A
formula produces:

Option A: (360 - ((sensor + user + 360) % 360)) % 360

  • sensor=270, user=0 (portrait): (360 - 270) % 360 = 90
  • So we rotate the source image 90° CW in the shader

The buffer shows the image rotated 270° CW from upright (which matches: upright source → rotated 90° CW in shader →
pixels are 90° CW from upright). Wait, actually looking at the buffer again...

Let me re-examine by reading "Venue: SCC 100" position. In the buffer, "Venue: SCC 100" runs vertically along the rightedge, reading from top to bottom. If the original poster is upright, that text would be at the top, reading left-to-
right. So the buffer has been rotated 90° CW from upright.

And the screen shows the image 180° upside-down (all text upside-down).

So native MIUI front camera takes our 90° CW buffer and displays it 180°. That means it applied +90° CW on top of our
buffer (90° + 90° = 180°). This is the same behavior as the back camera — native MIUI always adds 90° CW.

But wait — for the front camera, the standard Camera2 contract says the consumer should apply sensor_orientation = 270
(270° CW = 90° CCW). If native applied 270° CW to our 90° CW buffer: 90° + 270° = 360° = 0° (upright). But we see 180°,not upright. So native is NOT applying 270° CW.

Let me check what the f223d95 formula would produce for front camera:

  • ((360 - ((270 + 0 + 360) % 360)) + 180) % 360 = (90 + 180) % 360 = 270
  • Buffer would be 270° CW from upright
  • If native adds 90° CW: 270° + 90° = 360° = 0° → upright!

That confirms f223d95 was correct for front camera on native MIUI too. The native camera applies +90° CW to everything
(regardless of which camera), and f223d95's formula accounts for that.

Now I have both cameras' buffers and screens under Option A. Let me carefully derive the actual sensor orientations.

The key principle: A real hardware camera sensor is physically mounted rotated by SENSOR_ORIENTATION degrees CW relativeto the device's natural (portrait) orientation. So a real camera produces pixels that are rotated SENSOR_ORIENTATION
degrees CW from upright portrait.

Let me read the text orientations carefully:

Back camera (cam 0) — buffer:

  • "Venue: SCC 100" runs vertically along the LEFT edge, reading bottom-to-top
  • "Come And Join Us At The" is on the RIGHT edge reading top-to-bottom
  • This means the image is rotated 270° CW from upright (or equivalently 90° CCW)

Back camera (cam 0) — screen:

  • All text is upside-down (180°)

Front camera (cam 1) — buffer:

  • "Venue: SCC 100" runs vertically along the RIGHT edge, reading top-to-bottom
  • "Come And Join Us At The" is on the LEFT edge reading bottom-to-top
  • This means the image is rotated 90° CW from upright

Front camera (cam 1) — screen:

  • All text is upside-down (180°)

Now, Option A formula: (360 - ((sensor + user) % 360)) % 360

  • Back (sensor=90, user=0): shader rotation = 270° CW
  • Front (sensor=270, user=0): shader rotation = 90° CW

The shader applies this rotation to the upright source image. So:

  • Back buffer = upright + 270° CW = 270° CW from upright ✓ (matches what we see)
  • Front buffer = upright + 90° CW = 90° CW from upright ✓ (matches what we see)

Now, what should a real sensor produce?

A real sensor with SENSOR_ORIENTATION = X produces pixels that are X° CW from upright. So:

  • Real back sensor (SENSOR_ORIENTATION=90) → buffer should be 90° CW from upright
  • Real front sensor (SENSOR_ORIENTATION=270) → buffer should be 270° CW from upright

But Option A produces the OPPOSITE:

  • Back: 270° CW instead of 90° CW
  • Front: 90° CW instead of 270° CW

This is exactly why we see 180° on screen. Native MIUI applies the standard correction (rotate by SENSOR_ORIENTATION
CCW, i.e. 360 - SENSOR_ORIENTATION CW):

  • Back: buffer 270° + correction 270° CW (=360-90) = 540° = 180° ← upside-down ✓
  • Front: buffer 90° + correction 90° CW (=360-270) = 180° ← upside-down ✓

Both show 180° because Option A is exactly 180° off from real hardware in both cases.

Now let's verify f223d95's formula:

  • ((360 - ((sensor + user) % 360)) + 180) % 360
  • Back: (270 + 180) % 360 = 90° → buffer is 90° CW from upright → matches real sensor_orientation=90 ✓
  • Front: (90 + 180) % 360 = 270° → buffer is 270° CW from upright → matches real sensor_orientation=270 ✓

❭ why are the commands failing to capture buffers when virtualcam is off, i wanted us to capture real hardware buffers
  when using scanner app plus screenshot plus hardware audit to solve the scanner issue

Good point — the buffer dumps come from FormatConverterBridge and BufferDumper, which are part of VirtuCam's hook code.When VirtuCam is disabled, those hooks don't run, so there's nothing to capture the buffer.

To capture what the real hardware camera produces (without VirtuCam), we need a different approach. The buffer dump toolonly works when our hooks are active and intercepting frames.

There are a few options:

  1. Keep VirtuCam ON but feed through real camera frames — we'd need a "passthrough" mode that doesn't inject custom
  media but still runs our hooks (including BufferDumper). This way we capture what the real sensor outputs.
  2. Use Android's built-in screencap + manual observation — we can't capture the raw buffer without hooks, but we CAN
  screenshot the scanner app with the real camera to see how it displays real hardware output. If the scanner shows real
  camera upright, then we know scanner DOES apply rotation correction (and our buffer is wrong). If the scanner shows
  real camera sideways too, then scanner is broken with real hardware too.
  3. Add a lightweight standalone buffer capture — but this would basically be reimplementing what our hooks already do.

Option 2 is the fastest and answers the key question: Does the scanner app display real camera output correctly?

If you point the real camera at something with clear orientation (like text on a screen), take a screenshot of the
scanner app with VirtuCam OFF, we'll immediately know whether the scanner's rotation issue is our bug or the scanner's
bug.

For the HardwareAuditLogger data — that captures CameraCharacteristics which are the same whether VirtuCam is on or off(we don't modify characteristics). So that data is already valid.

Want to try option 2 (screenshot scanner with VirtuCam off + real camera), or would you prefer I build a passthrough
mode so we can capture actual raw sensor buffers through our pipeline?

● Edited .\app\src\main\java\com\virtucam\hooks\BufferDumper.kt
  │  1 +      /**
  │  2 +       * Dump a YUV_420_888 Image from an ImageReader as a PNG.
  │  3 +       * Converts YUV→RGB in-place then saves. Used by passthrough spy to
  │  4 +       * capture real hardware camera buffers.
  │  5 +       */
  │  6 +      fun dumpYuvImage(image: android.media.Image, tag: String) {
  │  7 +          val w = image.width
  │  8 +          val h = image.height
  │  9 +          if (w <= 0 || h <= 0) return
  │ 10 +          try {
  │ 11 +              val planes = image.planes
  │ 12 +              val yBuf = planes[0].buffer
  │ 13 +              val uBuf = planes[1].buffer
  │ 14 +              val vBuf = planes[2].buffer
  │ 15 +              val yRowStride = planes[0].rowStride
  │ 16 +              val uvRowStride = planes[1].rowStride
  │ 17 +              val uvPixStride = planes[1].pixelStride
  │ 18 +
  │ 19 +              val argbInts = IntArray(w * h)
  │ 20 +              for (row in 0 until h) {
  │ 21 +                  for (col in 0 until w) {
  │ 22 +                      val yVal = (yBuf.get(row * yRowStride + col).toInt() and 0xFF)
  │ 23 +                      val uvRow = row / 2
  │ 24 +                      val uvCol = col / 2
  │ 25 +                      val uVal = (uBuf.get(uvRow * uvRowStride + uvCol * uvPixStride).toInt() and 0xFF) - 128
  │ 26 +                      val vVal = (vBuf.get(uvRow * uvRowStride + uvCol * uvPixStride).toInt() and 0xFF) - 128
  │ 27 +                      val r = (yVal + 1.370705f * vVal).toInt().coerceIn(0, 255)
  │ 28 +                      val g = (yVal - 0.337633f * uVal - 0.698001f * vVal).toInt().coerceIn(0, 255)
  │ 29 +                      val b = (yVal + 1.732446f * uVal).toInt().coerceIn(0, 255)
  │ 30 +                      argbInts[row * w + col] = (0xFF shl 24) or (r shl 16) or (g shl 8) or b
  │ 31 +                  }
  │ 32 +              }
  │ 33 +
  │ 34 +              val pkg = try {
  │ 35 +                  android.app.AndroidAppHelper.currentPackageName() ?: "unknown"
  │ 36 +              } catch (_: Throwable) { "unknown" }
  │ 37 +              val pid = android.os.Process.myPid()
  │ 38 +              val ts = SimpleDateFormat("yyyyMMdd_HHmmss", Locale.US).format(Date())
  │ 39 +              val filename = "${tag}_${pkg}_pid${pid}_${ts}.png"
  │ 40 +
  │ 41 +              Thread {
  │ 42 +                  try {
  │ 43 +                      val dir = File(DIR)
  │ 44 +                      if (!dir.exists()) dir.mkdirs()
  │ 45 +                      val bitmap = Bitmap.createBitmap(w, h, Bitmap.Config.ARGB_8888)
  │ 46 +                      bitmap.setPixels(argbInts, 0, w, 0, 0, w, h)
  │ 47 +                      val file = File(dir, filename)
  │ 48 +                      FileOutputStream(file).use { os ->
  │ 49 +                          bitmap.compress(Bitmap.CompressFormat.PNG, 100, os)
  │ 50 +                      }
  │ 51 +                      bitmap.recycle()
  │ 52 +                      Log.i(TAG, "Dumped YUV buffer to ${file.absolutePath} (${w}x${h})")
  │ 53 +                  } catch (e: Throwable) {
  │ 54 +                      Log.e(TAG, "dumpYuvImage failed", e)
  │ 55 +                  }
  │ 56 +              }.also {
  │ 57 +                  it.name = "VirtuCam-BufferDump-YUV"
  │ 58 +                  it.isDaemon = true
  │ 59 +                  it.start()
  │ 60 +              }
  │ 61 +          } catch (e: Throwable) {
  │ 62 +              Log.e(TAG, "dumpYuvImage conversion failed", e)
  │ 63 +          }
  │ 64 +      }
  │ 65 +
  └ 66        fun dumpRgba(width: Int, height: Int, rgba: ByteArray, tag: String) {

  │  6 +       * [PASSTHROUGH] Create a spy ImageReader that captures real hardware YUV frames
  │  7 +       * without replacing any of the app's surfaces. The spy surface is added to the
  │  8 +       * session alongside the app's real surfaces. Every 5 seconds it dumps a frame
  │  9 +       * as PNG via BufferDumper so we can see exactly what the real sensor produces.
  │ 10 +       *
  │ 11 +       * @param width  width to match one of the app's surfaces (for comparable data)
  │ 12 +       * @param height height to match
  │ 13 +       * @return the spy Surface to inject into the session's surface list
  │ 14 +       */
  │ 15 +      private fun createSpyImageReader(width: Int, height: Int): Surface? {
  │ 16 +          try {
  │ 17 +              // Clean up any previous spy
  │ 18 +              releaseSpyReader()
  │ 19 +
  │ 20 +              if (spyHandlerThread == null) {
  │ 21 +                  spyHandlerThread = HandlerThread("VirtuCam-SpyDump").apply { start() }
  │ 22 +                  spyHandler = Handler(spyHandlerThread!!.looper)
  │ 23 +              }
  │ 24 +
  │ 25 +              spyImageReader = ImageReader.newInstance(
  │ 26 +                  width, height,
  │ 27 +                  android.graphics.ImageFormat.YUV_420_888,
  │ 28 +                  4 // enough headroom for the HAL
  │ 29 +              )
  │ 30 +
  │ 31 +              spyImageReader!!.setOnImageAvailableListener({ reader ->
  │ 32 +                  var img: Image? = null
  │ 33 +                  try {
  │ 34 +                      img = reader.acquireLatestImage() ?: return@setOnImageAvailableListener
  │ 35 +                      val nowMs = System.currentTimeMillis()
  │ 36 +                      if (nowMs - lastSpyDumpMs > 5_000L) {
  │ 37 +                          lastSpyDumpMs = nowMs
  │ 38 +                          BufferDumper.dumpYuvImage(img, "hw_real_${width}x${height}")
  │ 39 +                          Log.d(TAG, "PASSTHROUGH: Dumped real hardware frame ${width}x${height}")
  │ 40 +                      }
  │ 41 +                  } catch (e: Throwable) {
  │ 42 +                      Log.e(TAG, "PASSTHROUGH: Spy listener error", e)
  │ 43 +                  } finally {
  │ 44 +                      try { img?.close() } catch (_: Throwable) {}
  │ 45 +                  }
  │ 46 +              }, spyHandler)
  │ 47 +
  │ 48 +              val surface = spyImageReader!!.surface
  │ 49 +              Log.e(TAG, "PASSTHROUGH: Created spy ImageReader ${width}x${height} YUV_420_888")
  │ 50 +              return surface
  │ 51 +          } catch (e: Throwable) {
  │ 52 +              Log.e(TAG, "PASSTHROUGH: Failed to create spy ImageReader", e)
  │ 53 +              return null
  │ 54 +          }
  │ 55 +      }
  │ 56 +
  │ 57 +      private fun releaseSpyReader() {
  │ 58 +          try { spyImageReader?.close() } catch (_: Throwable) {}
  │ 59 +          spyImageReader = null
  │ 60 +      }
